                  - generic [ref=e4543]:
                    - paragraph [ref=e4544]: Below is a discussion of several approaches for materializing channels at different time scales in Python, along with suggestions for a corresponding notebook structure. I’ll then propose a series of Markdown and code blocks that you can paste directly into your notebook.
                    - separator [ref=e4545]
                    - 'heading "Discussion: Approaches to Construct Multi-Timeframe Channels" [level=2] [ref=e4546]'
                    - paragraph [ref=e4547]: "There are two main approaches you can consider:"
                    - heading "1. Multi-Resolution ZigZag Approach" [level=3] [ref=e4548]
                    - paragraph [ref=e4549]:
                      - strong [ref=e4550]: "Idea:"
                    - list [ref=e4551]:
                      - listitem [ref=e4552]:
                        - paragraph [ref=e4553]: Use a finer-resolution ZigZag (or extrema detection) indicator on your base dataset (e.g., hourly bars).
                      - listitem [ref=e4554]:
                        - paragraph [ref=e4555]: Adjust the sensitivity (threshold) and minimum trend length to filter for significant price extremes.
                      - listitem [ref=e4556]:
                        - paragraph [ref=e4557]:
                          - strong [ref=e4558]: "For higher timeframes:"
                        - list [ref=e4559]:
                          - listitem [ref=e4560]:
                            - paragraph [ref=e4561]: Either (a) aggregate the base-level extremes into larger windows (e.g., take the subset of extrema over a sliding multi-day window) and then fit a regression line to these extremes
                          - listitem [ref=e4562]:
                            - paragraph [ref=e4563]: Or (b) run separate ZigZag indicators with different sensitivities/minTrendLength parameters that naturally “scale up” to capture the macro (weekly/daily) structure.
                    - paragraph [ref=e4564]:
                      - strong [ref=e4565]: "Pros:"
                    - list [ref=e4566]:
                      - listitem [ref=e4567]:
                        - paragraph [ref=e4568]: You can tune the thresholds to filter out noise at each scale.
                      - listitem [ref=e4569]:
                        - paragraph [ref=e4570]: "The approach is very flexible: by varying sensitivity, you essentially “zoom out” or “zoom in” on the price action."
                    - paragraph [ref=e4571]:
                      - strong [ref=e4572]: "Cons:"
                    - list [ref=e4573]:
                      - listitem [ref=e4574]:
                        - paragraph [ref=e4575]: It may be challenging to determine which set of pivots to use for channel construction if the market is choppy.
                      - listitem [ref=e4576]:
                        - paragraph [ref=e4577]: It might produce differing numbers of extreme points (and therefore channels) at each resolution unless carefully tuned.
                    - heading "2. Regression Channel Approach" [level=3] [ref=e4578]
                    - paragraph [ref=e4579]:
                      - strong [ref=e4580]: "Idea:"
                    - list [ref=e4581]:
                      - listitem [ref=e4582]:
                        - paragraph [ref=e4583]: Use a regression channel indicator that fits a linear regression line (the best fit line) on your price data over a certain lookback period.
                      - listitem [ref=e4584]:
                        - paragraph [ref=e4585]: Compute the standard deviation (or average absolute deviation) of prices from that regression line to set an upper and lower boundary.
                      - listitem [ref=e4586]:
                        - paragraph [ref=e4587]:
                          - strong [ref=e4588]: "Multiple resolutions:"
                        - list [ref=e4589]:
                          - listitem [ref=e4590]:
                            - paragraph [ref=e4591]: Compute regression channels on daily, hourly, and weekly (or any other frequency) data.
                          - listitem [ref=e4592]:
                            - paragraph [ref=e4593]: This gives you channels that adapt automatically to the trend and volatility at the chosen lookback period.
                    - paragraph [ref=e4594]:
                      - strong [ref=e4595]: "Pros:"
                    - list [ref=e4596]:
                      - listitem [ref=e4597]:
                        - paragraph [ref=e4598]: A regression channel is a well-known method for channel estimation and tends to be robust, especially if combined with volatility measures.
                      - listitem [ref=e4599]:
                        - paragraph [ref=e4600]: The boundaries are calculated mathematically (e.g., using standard deviation), so you avoid the potential subjectivity of picking which extremes to use.
                    - paragraph [ref=e4601]:
                      - strong [ref=e4602]: "Cons:"
                    - list [ref=e4603]:
                      - listitem [ref=e4604]:
                        - paragraph [ref=e4605]: The lookback period must be chosen carefully since too short a period might be overreactive while too long may lag the trend.
                      - listitem [ref=e4606]:
                        - paragraph [ref=e4607]: If the underlying data is very noisy or non-linear, the regression channel may not capture sudden trend changes well.
                    - heading "Combining Both Methods" [level=3] [ref=e4608]
                    - paragraph [ref=e4609]: "You might actually combine both ideas:"
                    - list [ref=e4610]:
                      - listitem [ref=e4611]:
                        - paragraph [ref=e4612]: Use a high-resolution ZigZag indicator (or extrema detection) to isolate the key turning points in the market.
                      - listitem [ref=e4613]:
                        - paragraph [ref=e4614]: On those filtered extreme points, then compute a regression channel to derive the channel boundaries.
                      - listitem [ref=e4615]:
                        - paragraph [ref=e4616]: This hybrid method gives you control over the pivot detection (through sensitivity settings) and the robustness of a regression channel.
                    - heading "Recommendations" [level=3] [ref=e4617]
                    - list [ref=e4618]:
                      - listitem [ref=e4619]:
                        - paragraph [ref=e4620]:
                          - strong [ref=e4621]: "For a robust initial implementation:"
                        - list [ref=e4622]:
                          - listitem [ref=e4623]:
                            - paragraph [ref=e4624]: Try running a regression channel on the close prices (or on the selected extreme points) for each timeframe.
                          - listitem [ref=e4625]:
                            - paragraph [ref=e4626]: Use different lookback windows for each timeframe (e.g., 5 days for micro, 20 days for meso, 60 days for macro) and compare the channels.
                      - listitem [ref=e4627]:
                        - paragraph [ref=e4628]:
                          - strong [ref=e4629]: "Alternatively:"
                        - list [ref=e4630]:
                          - listitem [ref=e4631]:
                            - paragraph [ref=e4632]: "Implement two versions in your notebook: one with a stand-alone Regression Channel and one with the multi-resolution ZigZag (with modified thresholds)."
                          - listitem [ref=e4633]:
                            - paragraph [ref=e4634]: Visually compare the channels overlaid on the price chart to determine which approach is more consistent for BTCUSDT.
                      - listitem [ref=e4635]:
                        - paragraph [ref=e4636]:
                          - strong [ref=e4637]: "Additional Filters:"
                        - list [ref=e4638]:
                          - listitem [ref=e4639]:
                            - paragraph [ref=e4640]: You might include ADX or volatility filters (like ATR) to avoid trading in sideways markets.
                          - listitem [ref=e4641]:
                            - paragraph [ref=e4642]: Consider a logic that only takes a trade when both the regression channel (or the ZigZag-derived channel) and a momentum indicator are aligned.
                    - separator [ref=e4643]

                        - text: "# Multi-Timeframe Channel Analysis Using ZigZag and Regression Channels"
                        - text: This notebook demonstrates methods to materialize price channels at different time scales on BTCUSDT (using Binance data).
                        - text: "We explore two primary approaches:"
                        - text: 1. **Multi-Resolution ZigZag Approach:**
                        - text: By filtering and aggregating extrema detected from a high-resolution ZigZag indicator, we derive channels on different timeframes.
                        - text: 2. **Regression Channel Approach:**
                        - text: By fitting linear regressions over selected lookback periods (or on filtered extreme points), we compute regression channels with upper and lower boundaries.
                        - text: We will compare and visualize these channels and discuss how to integrate them into a trading strategy.

                      - generic [ref=e4778]:
                        - text: "## Custom ZigZag Implementation"
                        - text: "Since the native QC ZigZag indicator did not provide the alternating extremes as desired, we implement a custom function (`classic_chart_zigzag()`) that computes the pivot points from the price series."
                        - text: "This function returns a list of pivots, where each pivot is a tuple `(time, price, sign)`, with:"
                        - text: "- `+1`: indicating a pivot **low**"
                        - text: "- `-1`: indicating a pivot **high**"
                        - text: These pivots will form the basis for our channel construction.
                    - separator [ref=e4779]
                    - 'heading "Cell F: Code – Custom ZigZag Function" [level=3] [ref=e4780]':
                      - strong [ref=e4781]: "Cell F: Code – Custom ZigZag Function"
                    - generic [ref=e4789]:
                      - generic [ref=e4791]:
                        - generic [ref=e4792]:
                          - img [ref=e4793]
                          - text: Python
                        - generic [ref=e4795]:
                          - button "Copier" [ref=e4796] [cursor=pointer]:
                            - img [ref=e4797]

                            - generic [ref=e4800]:

                      - generic [ref=e4807]:
                        - text: "def classic_chart_zigzag(df, thresholdPercent=0.05):"
                        - text: "\"\"\""
                        - text: Manually computes ZigZag pivots akin to typical charting platforms.
                        - text: df must have columns 'time' and 'close'.
                        - text: "Returns a list of pivots (time, price, sign):"
                        - text: +1 -> Low pivot; -1 -> High pivot.
                        - text: "\"\"\""
                        - text: "if len(df) < 2:"
                        - text: return []
                        - text: pivots = []
                        - text: "# Initialize with the first bar"
                        - text: firstBar = df.iloc[0]
                        - text: lastPivotPrice = firstBar['close']
                        - text: lastPivotTime = firstBar['time']
                        - text: "# Determine initial direction using the second bar"
                        - text: secondBar = df.iloc[1]
                        - text: "directionUp = secondBar['close'] > lastPivotPrice # if True, search for highs"
                        - text: lastSign = +1 if directionUp else -1
                        - text: pivots.append((lastPivotTime, lastPivotPrice, lastSign))
                        - text: currentExtremePrice = lastPivotPrice
                        - text: currentExtremeTime = lastPivotTime
                        - text: "for i in range(1, len(df)):"
                        - text: row = df.iloc[i]
                        - text: price = row['close']
                        - text: time = row['time']
                        - text: "if directionUp:"
                        - text: "# Update maximum extreme"
                        - text: "if price > currentExtremePrice:"
                        - text: currentExtremePrice = price
                        - text: currentExtremeTime = time
                        - text: "else:"
                        - text: retrace = 1.0 - (price / currentExtremePrice)
                        - text: "if retrace >= thresholdPercent:"
                        - text: "# Confirm the high pivot"
                        - text: pivots.append((currentExtremeTime, currentExtremePrice, -1))
                        - text: directionUp = False
                        - text: currentExtremePrice = price
                        - text: currentExtremeTime = time
                        - text: "else:"
                        - text: "# Update minimum extreme"
                        - text: "if price < currentExtremePrice:"
                        - text: currentExtremePrice = price
                        - text: currentExtremeTime = time
                        - text: "else:"
                        - text: rally = (price / currentExtremePrice) - 1.0
                        - text: "if rally >= thresholdPercent:"
                        - text: pivots.append((currentExtremeTime, currentExtremePrice, +1))
                        - text: directionUp = True
                        - text: currentExtremePrice = price
                        - text: currentExtremeTime = time
                        - text: "# Optionally, append the last extreme as final pivot"
                        - text: pivots.append((currentExtremeTime, currentExtremePrice, +1 if not directionUp else -1))
                        - text: return pivots
                        - text: "# Compute pivots on hourly bars"
                        - text: pivotList = classic_chart_zigzag(bars_df[['time','close']], thresholdPercent=0.05)
                        - text: print("Computed ZigZag Pivots:")
                        - text: "for pivot in pivotList[:5]:"
                        - text: print(pivot)

                        - text: fig = go.Figure()
                        - text: "# Plot the raw close prices"
                        - text: fig.add_trace(go.Scatter(
                        - text: x=bars_df['time'],
                        - text: y=bars_df['close'],
                        - text: mode='lines',
                        - text: name='Close Price',
                        - text: line=dict(color='blue')
                        - text: ))
                        - text: "# Build data for the pivot line (connect all pivots)"
                        - text: xline, yline = [], []
                        - text: "for dt, price, sign in pivotList:"
                        - text: xline.append(dt)
                        - text: yline.append(price)
                        - text: fig.add_trace(go.Scatter(
                        - text: x=xline,
                        - text: y=yline,
                        - text: mode='lines',
                        - text: name='Classic ZigZag',
                        - text: line=dict(color='orange')
                        - text: ))
                        - text: "# Scatter: high pivots (red) and low pivots (green)"
                        - text: high_x, high_y = [], []
                        - text: low_x, low_y = [], []
                        - text: "for dt, price, sign in pivotList:"
                        - text: "if sign < 0: # High pivot"
                        - text: high_x.append(dt)
                        - text: high_y.append(price)
                        - text: "else: # Low pivot"
                        - text: low_x.append(dt)
                        - text: low_y.append(price)
                        - text: fig.add_trace(go.Scatter(
                        - text: x=high_x,
                        - text: y=high_y,
                        - text: mode='markers',
                        - text: marker=dict(color='red', size=7),
                        - text: name='High Pivot'
                        - text: ))
                        - text: fig.add_trace(go.Scatter(
                        - text: x=low_x,
                        - text: y=low_y,
                        - text: mode='markers',
                        - text: marker=dict(color='green', size=7),
                        - text: name='Low Pivot'
                        - text: ))
                        - text: fig.update_layout(
                        - text: title='BTCUSDT Hourly - Classic ZigZag',
                        - text: xaxis_title='Time',
                        - text: yaxis_title='Price (USDT)'
                        - text: )
                        - text: fig.show()
                        - text: "# Plot the ZigZag indicator on hourly bars"
                        - text: plot_manual_zigzag(bars_df, pivotList)
                    - separator [ref=e4862]
                    - 'heading "Cell I: Markdown – Channel Construction Discussion" [level=3] [ref=e4863]':
                      - strong [ref=e4864]: "Cell I: Markdown – Channel Construction Discussion"
                    - generic [ref=e4872]:
                      - generic [ref=e4874]:
                        - generic [ref=e4875]:
                          - img [ref=e4876]
                          - text: Markdown
                        - button "Copier" [ref=e4879] [cursor=pointer]:
                          - img [ref=e4880]
                      - generic [ref=e4886]:
                        - text: "## Discussion: Constructing Channels at Different Timeframes"
                        - text: Now that we have pivot data from our custom ZigZag indicator, we need to decide how to construct channels from these extrema.
                        - text: "### Option A: Regression Channel on Filtered Pivots"
                        - text: "- **Method:** For each timeframe (e.g., weekly, daily, hourly), select the relevant pivot points (e.g., all high pivots for resistance, all low pivots for support) over a predefined lookback period."
                        - text: "- **Process:** Fit a linear regression line through these points and compute the standard deviation. The regression line is the channel's center, and the boundaries are defined as this line plus or minus a multiple of the standard deviation."
                        - text: "- **Pros:** Provides a smooth, statistically grounded channel."
                        - text: "- **Cons:** May smooth out sudden reversals."
                        - text: "### Option B: Multi-Resolution ZigZag Filtering"
                        - text: "- **Method:** Run separate ZigZag indicators with different sensitivities for weekly, daily, and hourly data."
                        - text: "- **Process:** Use a higher threshold for the weekly (macro) channel and a lower threshold for the hourly (micro) channel. You can then combine these to decide whether a new channel is forming."
                        - text: "- **Pros:** More directly reflects the pivot structure."
                        - text: "- **Cons:** Sensitive to parameter selection; may produce very different pivot counts."
                        - text: "### Recommendation:"
                        - text: A good starting point is to experiment with **Option A (Regression Channel)** on the extremes extracted via our custom ZigZag. This combines the clarity of the regression channel with the filtered pivot points that capture the significant turning points. Later, you can compare with Option B or even hybridize both methods.
                        - text: Let's first focus on building a regression channel for the daily bars using the daily pivots.
                    - separator [ref=e4887]
                    - 'heading "Cell J: Code – Compute and Plot a Regression Channel on Daily Pivots" [level=3] [ref=e4888]':
                      - strong [ref=e4889]: "Cell J: Code – Compute and Plot a Regression Channel on Daily Pivots"
                    - generic [ref=e4897]:
                      - generic [ref=e4899]:
                        - generic [ref=e4900]:
                          - img [ref=e4901]
                          - text: Python
                        - generic [ref=e4903]:
                          - button "Copier" [ref=e4904] [cursor=pointer]:
                            - img [ref=e4905]
                          - button "Exécuter le code" [ref=e4907] [cursor=pointer]:
                            - generic [ref=e4908]:
                              - img [ref=e4909]
                              - text: Exécuter
                      - generic [ref=e4915]:
                        - text: import statsmodels.api as sm
                        - text: import matplotlib.pyplot as plt
                        - text: "def compute_regression_channel(pivot_df, multiplier=1.5):"
                        - text: "\"\"\""
                        - text: Given a DataFrame 'pivot_df' with columns ['time', 'price'],
                        - text: fit a linear regression and compute upper/lower channel boundaries.
                        - text: "The boundaries are set as:"
                        - text: center line ± (multiplier * std_residual)
                        - text: "\"\"\""
                        - text: "# Convert time to a numeric value (e.g., timestamp)"
                        - text: pivot_df = pivot_df.copy()
                        - text: pivot_df['timestamp'] = pivot_df['time'].astype(np.int64) // 10 ** 9
                        - text: X = pivot_df['timestamp']
                        - text: "X = sm.add_constant(X) # add intercept"
                        - text: Y = pivot_df['price']
                        - text: model = sm.OLS(Y, X).fit()
                        - text: pivot_df['fitted'] = model.predict(X)
                        - text: pivot_df['residual'] = pivot_df['price'] - pivot_df['fitted']
                        - text: std_resid = pivot_df['residual'].std()
                        - text: pivot_df['upper'] = pivot_df['fitted'] + multiplier * std_resid
                        - text: pivot_df['lower'] = pivot_df['fitted'] - multiplier * std_resid
                        - text: return pivot_df, model
                        - text: "# Let's extract daily low pivots from dailyPivotDict"
                        - text: daily_low_pivots = [ (dt, price) for dt, price, in zip(dailyData['time'], dailyData['close'])
                        - text: if dailyPivotDict.get(dt, PivotPointType.None) == PivotPointType.Low ]
                        - text: "# For simplicity, let's build a DataFrame from our daily data and include pivot info:"
                        - text: daily_data = dailyData.copy()
                        - text: "# In our earlier BuildPivotDict, we recorded the entire day's pivot."
                        - text: "# Here, we assume dailyPivotDict keys are the same as dailyData times."
                        - text: daily_pivots = pd.DataFrame([
                        - text: "{'time': dt, 'price': daily_data.loc[daily_data['time'] == dt, 'close'].values[0]}"
                        - text: for dt in dailyData['time'] if dailyPivotDict.get(dt, PivotPointType.None) == PivotPointType.Low
                        - text: "])"
                        - text: "if not daily_pivots.empty:"
                        - text: reg_channel, model = compute_regression_channel(daily_pivots)
                        - text: plt.figure(figsize=(10,6))
                        - text: plt.plot(daily_data['time'], daily_data['close'], label="Daily Close")
                        - text: plt.scatter(daily_pivots['time'], daily_pivots['price'], color='green', label="Daily Low Pivots")
                        - text: plt.plot(reg_channel['time'], reg_channel['fitted'], label="Regression Line", color='orange')
                        - text: plt.plot(reg_channel['time'], reg_channel['upper'], '--', label="Upper Channel", color='red')
                        - text: plt.plot(reg_channel['time'], reg_channel['lower'], '--', label="Lower Channel", color='red')
                        - text: plt.xlabel("Time")
                        - text: plt.ylabel("Price (USDT)")
                        - text: plt.title("Daily Regression Channel from Low Pivots")
                        - text: plt.legend()
                        - text: plt.show()
